## V17 PHOTO EXISTENCE LOGIC LIBRARY
### Source: modules/V17/PHOTO_EXISTENCE_LOGIC_LIBRARY.md
================================================================================

     1|# PHOTO EXISTENCE LOGIC LIBRARY
     2|### V17 — Why This Photo Exists
     3|### Status: ACTIVE — Runtime System
     4|
     5|---
     6|
     7|## PHILOSOPHY
     8|
     9|**Core Rule:** Every generated image MUST have a believable reason to exist.
    10|
    11|AI-generated images fail the "would this photo be taken?" test. The subject stares beautifully into nothing. The moment has no purpose. The viewer senses it immediately — the image has no existential justification.
    12|
    13|**The Fix:** Anchor every image to a real human behavior that generates the photo naturally.
    14|
    15|---
    16|
    17|## EXISTENCE LOGIC TEMPLATE
    18|
    19|Every prompt layer 2-4 should include ONE existence reason:
    20|
    21|```
    22|BECAUSE [human behavior] → [photo type] → [believable context]
    23|```
    24|
    25|---
    26|
    27|## EXISTENCE REASONS BY SPACE
    28|
    29|### 🏨 HOTEL ROOM
    30|
    31|| Reason | Trigger | Visible Evidence |
    32||--------|---------|------------------|
    33|| Outfit check before leaving | Standing at mirror, phone tilted | Phone in hand, mirror reflection, one shoe on |
    34|| Just woke up, phone check | In bed, morning light, blanket up | Phone on chest, squinting, unmade bed |
    35|| Waiting for friend | Sitting on bed edge, bored pose | Key card on table, door closed, one bag packed |
    36|| Post-shower, towel dry | Bathroom, steam, mirror fog | Wet hair dark, towel on shoulder, robe |
    37|| Late night room service | On bed, tray on lap, TV on | Half-eaten food, remote, late-night lighting |
    38|| Just arrived, still wearing travel clothes | Standing by window, backpack on | Carry-on visible, passport on desk, shoes still on |
    39|| Testing new swimsuit fit | In room, different angles | Full-length mirror, multiple bags visible |
    40|
    41|### 🌊 BEACH / POOL
    42|
    43|| Reason | Trigger | Visible Evidence |
    44||--------|---------|------------------|
    45|| Checking fit of new swimsuit | Turning to see back | Phone held, checking reflection |
    46|| Resting after swimming | Towel recline, tired expression | Wet hair flattened, body still wet |
    47|| Applying sunscreen to back | Arms behind, reaching | Bottle visible, mirror or friend behind |
    48|| Just out of water, cold | Shivering, skin goosebumps | Wet skin, towel being held |
    49|| Waiting for friends to arrive | Alone on beach, looking at phone | Chair reserved, bags, looking toward path |
    50|| Killing time, scrolling phone | Sitting on towel, casual | Phone in hand, bag nearby, half-drunk water |
    51|| Putting on cover-up | Just stood up from towel | One leg dressed, one not, sand on feet |
    52|
    53|### 🚇 MTR / PUBLIC TRANSIT
    54|
    55|| Reason | Trigger | Visible Evidence |
    56||--------|---------|------------------|
    57|| Waiting for MTR | Standing on platform, bored | Octopus card in hand, looking at arrival board |
    58|| Killing time between transfers | Sitting in corridor | Shopping bag, waiting expression |
    59|| Just got off MTR, checking phone | Standing in car, doors open | Phone in hand, one bag, about to exit |
    60|| Late night MTR alone | Sitting, tired | Headphones, minimal bags, empty car |
    61|| MTR too crowded, standing | Standing with pole, annoyed | Pole grip, near door, peak hour |
    62|| Taking MTR to meet friends | Looking at phone | Dressed up, bag, pre-event |
    63|| MTR exit, checking directions | Looking up at signs | Map on phone, confused expression |
    64|
    65|### 🏠 APARTMENT / HOME
    66|
    67|| Reason | Trigger | Visible Evidence |
    68||--------|---------|------------------|
    69|| Post-shower, getting ready | Bathroom mirror, steam | Towel on head, skincare visible |
    70|| Testing new outfit | Standing in bedroom mirror | Full-length mirror, multiple outfit choices on bed |
    71|| Morning coffee routine | Kitchen, lazy morning | Mug in hand, pajamas, morning light |
    72|| Bored on couch | Lying on couch, phone above | Lazy posture, TV on in background |
    73|| Late night snack | Kitchen counter, fridge open | Fridge light, snack in hand |
    74|| Sunday morning in bed | Just woke up, blanket | Morning light, unmade bed, no makeup |
    75|| Sending photo to boyfriend | In bedroom, preparing to send | Phone in hand, mirror angle, expression of anticipation |
    76|| Just bought new clothes, trying on | In room, bags still visible | Shopping bags, scattered clothes |
    77|
    78|### ☕ CAFÉ / RESTAURANT
    79|
    80|| Reason | Trigger | Visible Evidence |
    81||--------|---------|------------------|
    82|| Waiting for food | Phone on table, looking up | Place setting, waiting expression |
    83|| Killing time between appointments | Solo table, coffee | Book or phone, no food yet |
    84|| Friend photo for social media | Friend taking photo | Looking at friend, not camera, café background |
    85|| Testing makeup before date | Bathroom mirror | Makeup spread, phone propped |
    86|| Just ordered, food arriving | Excited expression | Server approaching, anticipation |
    87|
    88|### 🌃 STREET / OUTDOOR
    89|
    90|| Reason | Trigger | Visible Evidence |
    91||--------|---------|------------------|
    92|| Waiting for Uber | Standing on street, checking phone | Car app open, looking at road |
    93|| Taking photo of outfit of the day | Street mirror or reflective surface | Phone angled, checking reflection |
    94|| Resting after shopping | Bench, shopping bags | Multiple bags, sitting tired |
    95|| Meeting friends at landmark | Standing, looking for them | Scanning crowd, waiting expression |
    96|| Just got haircut | In front of salon mirror | Different hair, checking angles |
    97|| Trying on sunglasses | At display | Glasses on face, phone for comparison |
    98|
    99|### 🏨 HOT SPRING / ONSEN
   100|
   101|| Reason | Trigger | Visible Evidence |
   102||--------|---------|------------------|
   103|| Cooling off after bath | At outdoor onsen edge | Steam, towel on head, flushed skin |
   104|| Post-bath robe moment | Walking to room | Yukata, wooden sandals, relaxed |
   105|| Testing new hairstyle post-bath | Mirror in changing area | Wet hair, natural expression |
   106|
   107|---
   108|
   109|## INTEGRATION RULES
   110|
   111|### Rule 1: Existence Reason MUST Be in Layers 2-4
   112|
   113|```
   114|GOOD: "Post-swim rest on beach towel — friend just went to buy drinks, alone on beach, killing time"
   115|BAD: "Model on beach in swimsuit"
   116|```
   117|
   118|### Rule 2: Evidence Must Be Visible
   119|
   120|The existence reason should produce visual evidence:
   121|- Phone in hand = photo being taken/sent
   122|- One shoe on = just woke up or about to leave
   123|- Half-drunk water = been here a while
   124|- Key card on table = just arrived or about to check out
   125|
   126|### Rule 3: Expression Matches Reason
   127|
   128|| Reason | Expression |
   129||--------|------------|
   130|| Waiting for someone | Scanning, checking phone |
   131|| Just arrived | Alert, looking around |
   132|| Resting | Relaxed, eyes half-closed |
   133|| Preparing to send | Anticipating, slight smile |
   134|| Bored | Distant gaze, neutral |
   135|
   136|### Rule 4: Combine With Camera Awareness
   137|
   138|- **Existence + Level 1:** Friend asked for photo → subject knows, still natural
   139|- **Existence + Level 2:** Checking outfit → friend is there, they see it too
   140|- **Existence + Level 3:** Sending to boyfriend → subject in moment, phone dominant
   141|- **Existence + Level 4:** Documentary of journey → subject unaware, behavior natural
   142|
   143|### Rule 5: Avoid Staged Reasons
   144|
   145|```
   146|AVOID: "Posing for photo"
   147|GOOD: "Checking how her hair looks after the wind"
   148|GOOD: "Waiting for Uber, checking app"
   149|GOOD: "Looking up from phone because she heard her name"
   150|```
   151|
   152|---
   153|
   154|## COMPOUND EXISTENCE EXAMPLES
   155|
   156|### Beach Sending Photo
   157|```
   158|BECAUSE: Testing new swimsuit fit, sending photo to boyfriend
   159|→ Front camera angle, phone visible
   160|→ Slightly self-conscious but excited expression
   161|→ Beach towel in frame as context
   162|→ FRIEND-SHOT (friend took photo)
   163|```
   164|
   165|### MTR Late Night
   166|```
   167|BECAUSE: Late night MTR home after drinks, tired
   168|→ Empty car, headphones in, eyes closed
   169|→ One shopping bag on lap
   170|→ Looking exhausted but peaceful
   171|→ FORGOTTEN-CAMERA (accidental capture by surveillance or friend)
   172|```
   173|
   174|### Hotel Mirror Check
   175|```
   176|BECAUSE: Checking outfit before going out with friends
   177|→ Standing at hotel mirror, one shoe on
   178|→ Phone in hand (taking reference photo)
   179|→ Key card visible on table
   180|→ Full-length mirror capturing dress
   181|→ CAMERA-SELFIESQUE (phone is the camera)
   182|```
   183|
   184|### Post-Shower Apartment
   185|```
   186|BECAUSE: Just showered after beach, phone check in bedroom
   187|→ Hair wet and dark, towel on shoulders
   188|→ Still wearing cover-up or robe
   189|→ Morning light from window
   190|→ Skincare routine visible on desk
   191|→ LEVEL 3 (not performing, just existing)
   192|```
   193|
   194|---
   195|
   196|## ANTI-AI COMPOUND
   197|
   198|Combine with memory systems for maximum believability:
   199|
   200|```
   201|EXIST-01 (Photo Existence) + MEM-03 (Emotional Timing)
   202|→ Photo exists because of human behavior, moment captured mid-behavior
   203|
   204|EXIST-02 (Existence Evidence) + FAB-01 (Fabric Physics)  
   205|→ Physical evidence visible, fabric shows real wear
   206|
   207|EXIST-03 (Existence + Expression) + COL-02 (Fuji Pro 400H)
   208|→ Natural moment with dreamy film rendering
   209|```
   210|
   211|---
   212|
   213|## QUICK REFERENCE CARD
   214|
   215|**When generating:** Ask — "Would someone actually take this photo? Why?"
   216|
   217|**If no reason:** Add one from this library.
   218|
   219|**If reason is weak:** Strengthen with visible evidence.
   220|
   221|**Expression must match:** Waiting ≠ excited, tired ≠ alert.
   222|
   223|---
   224|
   225|*End of PHOTO_EXISTENCE_LOGIC_LIBRARY.md*
   226|

================================================================================
## V17 SPATIAL COMPOSITION LIBRARY
### Source: modules/V17/SPATIAL_COMPOSITION_LIBRARY.md
================================================================================

     1|# SPATIAL COMPOSITION LIBRARY
     2|### V17 — Foreground / Subject / Background Relationships
     3|### Status: ACTIVE — Runtime System
     4|
     5|---
     6|
     7|## PHILOSOPHY
     8|
     9|**Core Problem:** AI-generated images treat background as flat wallpaper behind the subject. Real photography has spatial depth — things exist at different distances from camera.
    10|
    11|**The Fix:** Every image needs foreground / subject / background STRUCTURE that creates real spatial depth.
    12|
    13|---
    14|
    15|## DEPTH LAYER SYSTEM
    16|
    17|### Three-Zone Spatial Model
    18|
    19|```
    20|┌─────────────────────────────────────┐
    21|│  BACKGROUND    │  SUBJECT  │ FOREGROUND │
    22|│  (far plane)   │ (mid)     │ (near)     │
    23|│  40-60% frame  │ 30-40%    │ 5-15%      │
    24|└─────────────────────────────────────┘
    25|```
    26|
    27|**Background:** Sets location, provides context, often soft/diffused
    28|**Subject:** Clear focus, occupies mid-ground
    29|**Foreground:** Creates depth, frames subject, adds realism
    30|
    31|---
    32|
    33|## SPATIAL COMPOSITIONS BY SPACE
    34|
    35|### 🏖️ BEACH
    36|
    37|```
    38|BASELINE COMPOSITION:
    39|foreground: sand + towel corner + flip flops → subject: body reclined/sitting → background: ocean + sky
    40|
    41|PHOTO TYPE: REAR TOWEL SELFIE
    42|foreground: arm holding phone + towel edge
    43|→ subject: back of head + upper back visible
    44|→ background: ocean horizon, someone else's umbrella
    45|
    46|PHOTO TYPE: FRONT TOWEL REST
    47|foreground: half-drunk water bottle + sunscreen bottle
    48|→ subject: lying on stomach, chin on folded arms
    49|→ background: ocean with slight motion blur
    50|
    51|PHOTO TYPE: WALKING TO WATER
    52|foreground: wet feet + shallow sand ripples
    53|→ subject: full body from behind, approaching ocean
    54|→ background: ocean depth, horizon line
    55|
    56|PHOTO TYPE: BEACH CHAIR
    57|foreground: paperback book + sunglasses on chair arm
    58|→ subject: sitting in chair, looking at sea
    59|→ background: ocean + distant boat
    60|```
    61|
    62|### 🏨 HOTEL ROOM
    63|
    64|```
    65|BASELINE COMPOSITION:
    66|foreground: blanket folds at frame edge → subject: body on bed/standing → background: window + city/sea
    67|
    68|PHOTO TYPE: BEDROOM STANDING
    69|foreground: luggage open on floor + clothes spilling out
    70|→ subject: standing by window in outfit
    71|→ background: window light + city view
    72|
    73|PHOTO TYPE: BED RECLINE
    74|foreground: remote control + phone on mattress edge
    75|→ subject: upper body reclined against headboard
    76|→ background: pillow + headboard + window
    77|
    78|PHOTO TYPE: VANITY CHECK
    79|foreground: perfume bottle + jewelry on dresser
    80|→ subject: face in mirror reflection
    81|→ background: mirror frame + hotel room interior
    82|
    83|PHOTO TYPE: BALCONY MOMENT
    84|foreground: balcony railing + ashtray/coffee cup
    85|→ subject: leaning on railing, looking out
    86|→ background: cityscape or sea
    87|```
    88|
    89|### 🚇 MTR (Mass Transit Railway)
    90|
    91|```
    92|BASELINE COMPOSITION:
    93|foreground: handrail or pole + standing passenger legs → subject: seated/standing → background: train interior depth
    94|
    95|PHOTO TYPE: SEATED PASSENGER
    96|foreground: shopping bag at feet + octopusc card on knee
    97|→ subject: seated, looking at phone
    98|→ background: train door + reflection + other passengers
    99|
   100|PHOTO TYPE: PLATFORM WAIT
   101|foreground: yellow safety line + foot positioning
   102|→ subject: standing, looking at arrival board
   103|→ background: platform depth + approaching train light
   104|
   105|PHOTO TYPE: CORRIDOR WALK
   106|foreground: moving feet + floor reflections
   107|→ subject: walking away or toward, slight motion blur
   108|→ background: corridor depth + station signage
   109|
   110|PHOTO TYPE: ESCALATOR RIDER
   111|foreground: escalator handrail + step edge
   112|→ subject: standing on escalator, profile view
   113|→ background: escalator structure + station interior
   114|```
   115|
   116|### 🛏️ BEDROOM (Apartment)
   117|
   118|```
   119|BASELINE COMPOSITION:
   120|foreground: bedding folds + pillow edge → subject: face/upper body → background: window + curtains
   121|
   122|PHOTO TYPE: MORNING LIGHT
   123|foreground: tangled sheet + phone on mattress
   124|→ subject: face on pillow, morning light raking
   125|→ background: window with diffused light
   126|
   127|PHOTO TYPE: VANITY DRESSING
   128|foreground: scattered skincare + jewelry box open
   129|→ subject: at mirror, applying makeup
   130|→ background: mirror reflection + bedroom behind
   131|
   132|PHOTO TYPE: BED EDGE SIT
   133|foreground: blanket bunched at knee + phone charging cable
   134|→ subject: sitting on bed edge, looking at phone
   135|→ background: unmade bed + window
   136|
   137|PHOTO TYPE: CLOSET CHECK
   138|foreground: clothes on floor from earlier tries + shoe rack
   139|→ subject: standing in front of open closet
   140|→ background: closet interior + clothes visible
   141|```
   142|
   143|### ☕ CAFÉ / RESTAURANT
   144|
   145|```
   146|BASELINE COMPOSITION:
   147|foreground: cup edge + menu card → subject: upper body at table → background: café interior depth
   148|
   149|PHOTO TYPE: TABLE WAIT
   150|foreground: phone + keys + napkin holder
   151|→ subject: seated, looking up from phone
   152|→ background: window + street outside
   153|
   154|PHOTO TYPE: WINDOW SEAT
   155|foreground: condensation on glass + window frame edge
   156|→ subject: face against window, looking out
   157|→ background: street scene outside, soft bokeh
   158|
   159|PHOTO TYPE: FOOD ARRIVAL
   160|foreground: chopsticks in hand + bowl edge
   161|→ subject: leaning forward, excited about food
   162|→ background: table setting + friends or empty chair
   163|```
   164|
   165|### 🌃 STREET / NIGHT OUT
   166|
   167|```
   168|BASELINE COMPOSITION:
   169|foreground: pavement edge + object → subject: full/three-quarter → background: building lights + depth
   170|
   171|PHOTO TYPE: NEON REFLECTION
   172|foreground: puddle reflection + street lamp glow
   173|→ subject: standing in neon light, looking at phone
   174|→ background: neon signs + building facades
   175|
   176|PHOTO TYPE: ALLEYWAY MOMENT
   177|foreground: graffiti wall edge + motorbike
   178|→ subject: leaning against wall, smoking/sth
   179|→ background: alley depth + street light at end
   180|
   181|PHOTO TYPE: CROSSWALK WAIT
   182|foreground: crossing signal + pedestrian legs
   183|→ subject: waiting at line, looking at light
   184|→ background: stopped cars + building lights
   185|```
   186|
   187|### 🛁 BATHROOM
   188|
   189|```
   190|BASELINE COMPOSITION:
   191|foreground: sink edge + toiletries → subject: face in mirror → background: tile wall + towel rack
   192|
   193|PHOTO TYPE: POST-SHOWER
   194|foreground: steam on mirror + toothbrush holder
   195|→ subject: face visible through steam, towel on head
   196|→ background: shower curtain + tile
   197|
   198|PHOTO TYPE: MEDICINE CABINET CHECK
   199|foreground: skincare products + cotton pads
   200|→ subject: face in mirror, cabinet open behind
   201|→ background: cabinet interior + products
   202|```
   203|
   204|---
   205|
   206|## SPATIAL DEPTH TRIGGERS
   207|
   208|### FOREGROUND CREATION TECHNIQUES
   209|
   210|| Technique | Example | When to Use |
   211||-----------|---------|-------------|
   212|| Object at frame edge | Towel corner, shoe, bag | Beach, hotel, bedroom |
   213|| Body part cropped close | Feet, hands, shoulder | Intimate, voyeur, documentary |
   214|| Fabric in frame | Blanket fold, curtain | Indoor, domestic |
   215|| Environmental edge | Door frame, window frame | Indoor/outdoor transition |
   216|| Shadow as foreground | Shadow on floor | Any space with strong light |
   217|
   218|### BACKGROUND SOFTNESS CONTROL
   219|
   220|| Distance | Treatment | Example |
   221||----------|-----------|---------|
   222|| Far background | Strong bokeh | City lights, ocean |
   223|| Mid background | Soft focus | Building facade, wall |
   224|| Near background | Sharp | Furniture, curtains, plants |
   225|
   226|---
   227|
   228|## COMPOUND SPATIAL PATTERNS
   229|
   230|### BEACH + HOTEL (泳灘/酒店 combo)
   231|```
   232|foreground: hotel towel edge + sand grain detail
   233|→ subject: wearing beach cover-up, hotel balcony
   234|→ background: beach + ocean visible from height
   235|→ Spatial logic: "Just came from beach to hotel room"
   236|```
   237|
   238|### MTR + STREET (港鐵/街道 combo)
   239|```
   240|foreground: MTR pillar edge + yellow line
   241|→ subject: exiting MTR station, still underground
   242|→ background: station depth + street light ahead
   243|→ Spatial logic: "Just came up from MTR"
   244|```
   245|
   246|### BEDROOM + BALCONY (卧室/露台 combo)
   247|```
   248|foreground: bedroom door frame + hallway light
   249|→ subject: standing at balcony threshold
   250|→ background: balcony + city night view
   251|→ Spatial logic: "Transition from inside to outside"
   252|```
   253|
   254|---
   255|
   256|## ANTI-AI COMPOUND
   257|
   258|```
   259|SPATIAL-01 (Three-zone depth) + MEM-01 (Incomplete Framing)
   260|→ Foreground cut off naturally, background partly visible
   261|
   262|SPATIAL-02 (Foreground edge) + FAB-02 (Garment drape)
   263|→ Fabric in foreground creates real depth
   264|
   265|SPATIAL-03 (Background softness) + COL-02 (Fuji Pro 400H)
   266|→ Dreamy depth with soft background rendering
   267|
   268|SPATIAL-04 (Spatial logic) + EXIST-01 (Photo existence)
   269|→ Every depth layer justifies why photo exists
   270|```
   271|
   272|---
   273|
   274|## SPATIAL COMPOSITION RULES
   275|
   276|1. **Never flat background** — always 2-3 depth zones
   277|2. **Foreground at 5-15% frame** — enough to create depth, not block subject
   278|3. **Background provides context** — soft or sharp depending on mood
   279|4. **Subject is clear focus point** — mid-ground by default
   280|5. **Spatial logic must make sense** — objects at same depth behave similarly
   281|
   282|---
   283|
   284|## QUICK GENERATION RULE
   285|
   286|**Every image needs:**
   287|```
   288|FOREGROUND: [one object at frame edge]
   289|→ SUBJECT: [clear focus, mid-ground]
   290|→ BACKGROUND: [location context, depth treatment]
   291|```
   292|
   293|**If no spatial depth:** Add foreground element from this library.
   294|
   295|---
   296|
   297|*End of SPATIAL_COMPOSITION_LIBRARY.md*
   298|

================================================================================
## V17 POSE MECHANICS LIBRARY
### Source: modules/V17/POSE_MECHANICS_LIBRARY.md
================================================================================

     1|# POSE MECHANICS LIBRARY
     2|### V17 — How the Body Physically Arrives at Poses
     3|### Status: ACTIVE — Runtime System
     4|
     5|---
     6|
     7|## PHILOSOPHY
     8|
     9|**Core Problem:** AI-generated images show "poses" as static frozen positions — no understanding of how the human body gets there. The result is mannequins that look posed, not humans caught mid-behavior.
    10|
    11|**The Fix:** Describe the MECHANICS — how weight shifts, how joints rotate, how momentum carries through. Poses become BECOME-positions, not static poses.
    12|
    13|---
    14|
    15|## POSE MECHANICS VOCABULARY
    16|
    17|### Weight Transfer Phrases
    18|
    19|| Mechanic | Description | Visual Result |
    20||----------|-------------|---------------|
    21|| Weight shifts forward | Hip moves ahead of ankle | Forward lean, ready to move |
    22|| Weight settles back | Hip returns, body drops | Relaxed, grounded |
    23|| Weight goes one leg | Standing leg straight, other leg bent | Casual standing |
    24|| Weight sinks into surface | Gravity compresses buttocks | Natural sitting weight |
    25|| Weight redistributes | Feet shuffle, body adjusts | In-process movement |
    26|
    27|### Joint Rotation Phrases
    28|
    29|| Mechanic | Description | Visual Result |
    30||----------|-------------|---------------|
    31|| Pelvis rotates | Hips turn faster than shoulders | Twisted torso, tension |
    32|| Ribcage follows | Upper body catches up | Spiral line |
    33|| Shoulder leads | Arm goes first, body follows | Reaching, throwing |
    34|| Head turns last | Neck twists after body | Over-the-shoulder look |
    35|| Knee bends first | Leg folds before body sits | Sitting preparation |
    36|
    37|### Muscle Engagement Phrases
    38|
    39|| Mechanic | Description | Visual Result |
    40||----------|-------------|---------------|
    41|| Core stabilizes | Stomach tightens | Flat back, balance |
    42|| Glutes activate | Standing leg firm | Weight-bearing visible |
    43|| Shoulder lifts | Trapezius engages | Raised arm, shrug |
    44|| Neck extends | Head tilts back | Looking up, stretching |
    45|
    46|---
    47|
    48|## POSE MECHANICS BY TYPE
    49|
    50|### 1. SITTING ON EDGE
    51|
    52|**Mechanics Sequence:**
    53|```
    54|1. Approach surface
    55|2. One hand reaches back to feel for edge
    56|3. Knee bends, body lowers
    57|4. Weight sinks into sit-bone
    58|5. Feet plant for balance
    59|6. Torso settles, spine curves
    60|```
    61|
    62|**Pose Descriptions (use these, not "sitting pose"):**
    63|- "Lowered onto edge, one hand still reaching back"
    64|- "Weight sinking into mattress, spine still straight"
    65|- "Just felt edge, knees bent, about to sit"
    66|- "Settled into seat, lower back against chair"
    67|
    68|**Avoid:** "sitting elegantly" / "model sits on chair"
    69|
    70|---
    71|
    72|### 2. LYING ON STOMACH
    73|
    74|**Mechanics Sequence:**
    75|```
    76|1. Knees touch surface first
    77|2. Hands plant for support
    78|3. Hips shift forward over knees
    79|4. Torso lowers, elbows bend
    80|5. Chin comes to rest on folded arms
    81|6. Pelvis relaxes, weight drops
    82|```
    83|
    84|**Pose Descriptions:**
    85|- "Knees on towel, arms folded under chin, pelvis dropped"
    86|- "Upper body lowered onto forearms, hip still slightly raised"
    87|- "Relaxed onto stomach, cheek on pillow, one knee bent"
    88|- "Getting comfortable on towel, arms adjusting"
    89|
    90|---
    91|
    92|### 3. LEANING ON SURFACE
    93|
    94|**Mechanics Sequence:**
    95|```
    96|1. One leg steps back, foot plants
    97|2. Hip shifts back toward surface
    98|3. Upper body leans, shoulder touches wall/object
    99|4. Arm reaches to brace or rest
   100|5. Head tilts toward surface
   101|6. Weight distributes through lean
   102|```
   103|
   104|**Pose Descriptions:**
   105|- "Hip shifting back to wall, shoulder making contact"
   106|- "Leg stepped back for balance, upper body tipping into rail"
   107|- "One arm braced on railing, weight tipping forward"
   108|- "Shoulder against window, head following toward glass"
   109|
   110|---
   111|
   112|### 4. WALKING / MOVING
   113|
   114|**Mechanics Sequence:**
   115|```
   116|1. Back foot pushes off ground
   117|2. Weight transfers to front foot
   118|3. Hip rotates forward
   119|4. Opposite arm swings forward
   120|5. Head leads slightly into direction
   121|6. Momentum carries body through frame
   122|```
   123|
   124|**Pose Descriptions:**
   125|- "Mid-step, back foot pushing off, front foot landing"
   126|- "Momentum carrying forward, arm swinging opposite to leg"
   127|- "Walking toward camera, hip rotation visible"
   128|- "Stepping off curb, slight bob, weight not yet settled"
   129|
   130|---
   131|
   132|### 5. REACHING FOR SOMETHING
   133|
   134|**Mechanics Sequence:**
   135|```
   136|1. Eyes find target
   137|2. Shoulder retracts, arm lifts
   138|3. Hand extends toward object
   139|4. Body leans in direction of reach
   140|5. Opposite arm counterbalances
   141|6. Fingers approach, adjustment micro-movements
   142|```
   143|
   144|**Pose Descriptions:**
   145|- "Shoulder lifting, arm reaching toward phone on table"
   146|- "Body leaning forward, hand closing distance to glass"
   147|- "Arm extended, fingers adjusting angle to grab cup"
   148|- "Reaching up to shelf, opposite hand steadying hip"
   149|
   150|---
   151|
   152|### 6. TURNING TO LOOK
   153|
   154|**Mechanics Sequence:**
   155|```
   156|1. Eyes move first, find target
   157|2. Head follows, neck rotates
   158|3. Shoulder on opposite side lifts slightly
   159|4. Upper back rotates
   160|5. Lower body stays or minimal rotation
   161|6. Result: three-quarter view
   162|```
   163|
   164|**Pose Descriptions:**
   165|- "Head mid-turn, neck still rotating, body still forward"
   166|- "Shoulder lifting as head turns back over shoulder"
   167|- "Half-turned, pelvis still facing original direction"
   168|- "Over-the-shoulder look, neck tension visible"
   169|
   170|---
   171|
   172|### 7. LYING ON BACK
   173|
   174|**Mechanics Sequence:**
   175|```
   176|1. Back of knees touches surface
   177|2. Body lowers backward
   178|3. Head follows, pillow receives
   179|4. Arms settle to sides or overhead
   180|5. Pelvis releases, spine settles
   181|6. Breath exhale, shoulders drop
   182|```
   183|
   184|**Pose Descriptions:**
   185|- "Back lowering toward mattress, knees still bent"
   186|- "Head touching pillow, arms settling to sides"
   187|- "Knees up, back still arched, not yet relaxed"
   188|- "Weight sinking into surface, breath half-out"
   189|
   190|---
   191|
   192|### 8. SQUATTING
   193|
   194|**Mechanics Sequence:**
   195|```
   196|1. Feet shoulder-width or wider
   197|2. Knees bend, hips push back
   198|3. Torso leans slightly forward for balance
   199|4. Arms extend for balance
   200|5. Weight drops into heels
   201|6. Lower back maintains neutral curve
   202|```
   203|
   204|**Pose Descriptions:**
   205|- "Knees bent, hips dropping, heel contact firm"
   206|- "Squatting at beach towel edge, about to sit fully"
   207|- "Heels planted, torso leaning forward for balance"
   208|- "Low squat, knees out, weight in heels"
   209|
   210|---
   211|
   212|### 9. CLIMBING / STEPPING
   213|
   214|**Mechanics Sequence:**
   215|```
   216|1. Foot lifts, toes point up
   217|2. Shin lifts toward knee
   218|3. Thigh raises, knee leads
   219|4. Foot reaches for surface
   220|5. Weight transfers, standing leg activates
   221|6. Back leg follows through
   222|```
   223|
   224|**Pose Descriptions:**
   225|- "Foot on step, weight shifting forward, back leg straight"
   226|- "Mid-step onto curb, shin vertical, heel lifting"
   227|- "Climbing out of pool, hands gripping edge, leg pushing up"
   228|- "Stepping over threshold, toe contact first, heel follows"
   229|
   230|---
   231|
   232|### 10. LYING ON SIDE
   233|
   234|**Mechanics Sequence:**
   235|```
   236|1. One shoulder drops toward surface
   237|2. Upper arm follows, head settles
   238|3. Lower body lowers, hip then knee
   239|4. Body curls into fetal-adjacent
   240|5. Top knee bends forward
   241|6. Spine curves, weight on hip point
   242|```
   243|
   244|**Pose Descriptions:**
   245|- "Lowered onto side, hip taking weight, knee following"
   246|- "Side position, top knee bent forward, head on pillow"
   247|- "Curled on side, spine curved, shoulder relaxed"
   248|- "Turning to side, arm still under head"
   249|
   250|---
   251|
   252|## POSE MECHANICS INTEGRATION RULES
   253|
   254|### Rule 1: Describe the Becoming, Not the Been
   255|
   256|```
   257|BAD: "Subject sitting on bed"
   258|GOOD: "Weight lowering onto bed edge, hand reaching back to feel mattress"
   259|```
   260|
   261|### Rule 2: Include One Micro-Movement
   262|
   263|Every pose should have one element of in-progress movement:
   264|- "Knee about to bend"
   265|- "Hand not yet landed"
   266|- "Weight not yet fully transferred"
   267|- "Breath half-inhaled"
   268|
   269|### Rule 3: Connect to the Surface
   270|
   271|Real poses involve body responding to surface:
   272|- Hand reaching for chair
   273|- Feet planted for sitting
   274|- Shoulder against wall
   275|- Back against headboard
   276|
   277|### Rule 4: Chain the Sequence
   278|
   279|Describe 2-3 steps in the chain:
   280|```
   281|"Foot lifted, shin raising, knee leading toward surface, body lowering, weight not yet settled"
   282|```
   283|
   284|### Rule 5: Avoid Static Pose Keywords
   285|
   286|Replace these:
   287|- ❌ "posed" → ✅ "weight settling"
   288|- ❌ "standing" → ✅ "standing on one leg, other foot shifting"
   289|- ❌ "lying down" → ✅ "back lowering, pillow receiving head"
   290|- ❌ "leaning" → ✅ "hip shifting back toward wall"
   291|
   292|---
   293|
   294|## COMPOUND POSE MECHANICS EXAMPLES
   295|
   296|### Beach Recline
   297|```
   298|Mechanics: Knees on towel → hands planting → hips shifting forward → torso lowering → elbows bending → chin on forearms
   299|→ Result: Relaxed stomach-down on beach towel, not "posing"
   300|```
   301|
   302|### Hotel Bed Morning
   303|```
   304|Mechanics: Back of head lowering → pillow receiving → arm reaching for phone → eyes squinting
   305|→ Result: Morning moment, not "model in bed"
   306|```
   307|
   308|### MTR Standing
   309|```
   310|Mechanics: Foot stepping into car → body following through door → arm reaching for pole → balance stabilizing
   311|→ Result: Commuter in motion, not "standing model"
   312|```
   313|
   314|### Street Walking
   315|```
   316|Mechanics: Back foot pushing off → weight transferring → hip rotating → opposite arm swinging → head leading
   317|→ Result: Natural walk cycle, not "posing while walking"
   318|```
   319|
   320|---
   321|
   322|## ANTI-AI COMPOUND
   323|
   324|```
   325|POSE-01 (In-process mechanics) + MEM-03 (Emotional Timing)
   326|→ Pose caught mid-becoming, expression matches
   327|
   328|POSE-02 (Surface contact) + FAB-02 (Garment drape)
   329|→ Body mechanics visible through fabric behavior
   330|
   331|POSE-03 (Weight transfer) + DIS-05 (Forgotten camera)
   332|→ Natural body in motion, accidental capture
   333|
   334|POSE-04 (Micro-movement) + COL-02 (Fuji Pro 400H)
   335|→ Snapshot moment with dreamy rendering
   336|```
   337|
   338|---
   339|
   340|## QUICK REFERENCE CARD
   341|
   342|**When generating poses:** Ask — "How does the body physically get here?"
   343|
   344|**Use mechanics language:**
   345|- Weight shifts, sinks, drops
   346|- Joints rotate, bend, extend
   347|- Muscles activate, release
   348|- Surfaces receive, support
   349|
   350|**Always include one micro-movement:**
   351|- "about to..."
   352|- "still adjusting..."
   353|- "mid-transfer..."
   354|- "not yet settled..."
   355|
   356|---
   357|
   358|*End of POSE_MECHANICS_LIBRARY.md*
   359|

## V17 GARMENT PHYSICS LIBRARY
### Source: modules/V17/GARMENT_PHYSICS_LIBRARY.md
================================================================================

     1|# GARMENT PHYSICS LIBRARY
     2|### V17 — Layering, Gravity, and Fabric Behavior
     3|### Status: ACTIVE — Runtime System
     4|
     5|---
     6|
     7|## PHILOSOPHY
     8|
     9|**Core Problem:** AI-generated images show clothing as flat textures placed on bodies — no understanding of why fabric hangs, pools, drapes, or clings. Clothing exists in 3D space and responds to gravity, body posture, and layer interaction.
    10|
    11|**The Fix:** Describe WHY clothing looks the way it does — physics vocabulary that explains garment behavior. NOT "she's wearing an open cardigan" but "the cardigan's weight pulls it open, fabric falling away from shoulders under its own weight."
    12|
    13|---
    14|
    15|## FABRIC PHYSICS VOCABULARY
    16|
    17|### Gravity Effects
    18|
    19|| Mechanic | Description | Visual Result |
    20||----------|-------------|---------------|
    21|| Weight pull | Fabric sinks under own weight | Drape away from body, elongation |
    22|| Pooling | Fabric accumulates at lowest point | Gathering at hem, bunching |
    23|| Compression | Gravity + surface = flattening | Fabric thins, clings tight |
    24|| Stretching | Weight pulls, elasticity resists | Tension lines, transparency |
    25|| Sliding | Gravity overcomes friction | Fabric slipping, repositioning |
    26|
    27|### Body Interaction
    28|
    29|| Mechanic | Description | Visual Result |
    30||----------|-------------|---------------|
    31|| Contouring | Fabric follows body curve | Silhouette visible through fabric |
    32|| Gap creation | Body moves, fabric stays | Space between fabric and skin |
    33|| Pressure point | Body contacts surface | Fabric compression at contact |
    34|| Release | Pressure removed | Fabric expanding, returning |
    35|| Tension line | Pull from two directions | Fabric taut, lines radiating |
    36|
    37|### Layer Behavior
    38|
    39|| Mechanic | Description | Visual Result |
    40||----------|-------------|---------------|
    41|| Stacking | Upper layer weight on lower | Compression, creasing |
    42|| Exposure | Upper layer parts, reveals lower | Neckline gap, hem reveal |
    43|| Shadowing | Upper layer casts shadow | Lower layer darker |
    44|| Movement lag | Lower layer moves less | Different fabric behavior speeds |
    45|
    46|---
    47|
    48|## GARMENT PHYSICS BY TYPE
    49|
    50|### 1. OPEN CARDIGAN DRAPE
    51|
    52|**Physics Logic:**
    53|```
    54|Cardigan is heavy → gravity pulls down → front panels separate → 
    55|fabric falls away from torso → inner garment visible through opening → 
    56|shoulder seam visible → sleeves hang with less body contact
    57|```
    58|
    59|**Pose Descriptions:**
    60|- "Cardigan hanging open, front panels separated by gravity, inner shirt visible through gap"
    61|- "Cardigan's own weight pulling it away from body, shoulder seams exposed"
    62|- "Open cardigan fabric draping away from chest, weight making it hang rather than cling"
    63|- "Cardigan panels fallen forward, not styled open but gravity-determined"
    64|
    65|**Avoid:** "wearing cardigan open fashionably"
    66|
    67|---
    68|
    69|### 2. CAMISOLE LAYERING
    70|
    71|**Physics Logic:**
    72|```
    73|Thin fabric → contours body closely → reveals silhouette → 
    74|under-bust line visible → skin shows through slightly → 
    75|bra line may peek at edges → fabric moves with breath
    76|```
    77|
    78|**Pose Descriptions:**
    79|- "Thin camisole clinging to torso, body contour visible through fabric"
    80|- "Camisole draping over under-bust, fabric following ribcage curve"
    81|- "Sheer camisole, skin tone visible through fabric, chest rise with breath"
    82|- "Camisole shifting as body moves, fabric not stiff, fabric responding"
    83|
    84|**Avoid:** "sheer top" / "lace camisole" (without physics explanation)
    85|
    86|---
    87|
    88|### 3. LACE TRIM VISIBILITY
    89|
    90|**Physics Logic:**
    91|```
    92|Lace = pattern + holes → skin shows through openings → 
    93|lace lays flat when hanging → lace lifts when body moves → 
    94|lace catches shadow against skin → decorative AND functional
    95|```
    96|
    97|**Pose Descriptions:**
    98|- "Lace trim laying against skin, skin visible through pattern, shadow in openings"
    99|- "Lace edge lifting slightly from movement, pattern casting micro-shadows"
   100|- "Lace at neckline draping with fabric, not standing stiff, pattern open"
   101|- "Delicate lace following body curve, holes revealing skin beneath"
   102|
   103|---
   104|
   105|### 4. SHIRT SLEEVE SLIPPING
   106|
   107|**Physics Logic:**
   108|```
   109|Sleeve shoulder seam → rests at edge of shoulder → 
   110|arm movement reduces contact → gravity pulls sleeve down → 
   111|seam slides toward upper arm → shoulder becomes exposed → 
   112|more movement = more slippage
   113|```
   114|
   115|**Pose Descriptions:**
   116|- "Sleeve slipped from shoulder, seam resting on upper arm, shoulder exposed"
   117|- "Shirt sliding off shoulder, gravity and movement combined"
   118|- "Shoulder-baring moment, sleeve seam on upper arm, not styled"
   119|- "Sleeve falling forward on arm, weight pulling fabric down"
   120|
   121|**Avoid:** "off-shoulder styling" / "intentional bare shoulder"
   122|
   123|---
   124|
   125|### 5. WAISTBAND COMPRESSION
   126|
   127|**Physics Logic:**
   128|```
   129|Tight waistband → compresses soft tissue → fabric indents skin → 
   130|band creates visible line across torso → flesh above/below may bulge → 
   131|fabric smooth over compressed zone
   132|```
   133|
   134|**Pose Descriptions:**
   135|- "Waistband creating compression line, flesh slightly bulging above tight band"
   136|- "Skirt waistband cutting into skin, compression visible at seam"
   137|- "Tight band indenting torso, elastic creating body contour line"
   138|- "Waistband compressing fabric against skin, weight of garment showing"
   139|
   140|---
   141|
   142|### 6. SKIRT DISPLACEMENT FROM SITTING
   143|
   144|**Physics Logic:**
   145|```
   146|Body sits → hip angle changes → skirt fabric pushes backward → 
   147|fabric bunches at back waistband → front fabric pulls taut → 
   148|skirt appears shorter in front → back shows more fabric
   149|```
   150|
   151|**Pose Descriptions:**
   152|- "Skirt bunched at back from sitting, front fabric pulled taut"
   153|- "Sitting compression pushing skirt fabric back, bunching at waistband"
   154|- "Skirt displaced backward by sitting, front hem rising slightly"
   155|- "Hip angle changing skirt drape, fabric redistributed to back"
   156|
   157|**Avoid:** "short skirt" (focus on WHY it looks that way)
   158|
   159|---
   160|
   161|### 7. FABRIC POOLING AT HEM
   162|
   163|**Physics Logic:**
   164|```
   165|Long garment + standing = fabric pools at floor → 
   166|weight accumulates → creates gathered fabric mass → 
   167|some fabric spreads, some bunches → shadow cast on floor
   168|```
   169|
   170|**Pose Descriptions:**
   171|- "Dress fabric pooling on floor, accumulated weight creating mass"
   172|- "Hem fabric bunched at floor, sitting on itself"
   173|- "Long dress creating fabric puddle at feet, some spread, some gathered"
   174|- "Fabric gathering at lowest point, hem invisible under accumulated cloth"
   175|
   176|---
   177|
   178|### 8. NECKLINE GEOMETRY
   179|
   180|**Physics Logic:**
   181|```
   182|Neckline shape determined by → fabric weight + body posture + 
   183|gravity direction + chest position → front neckline pulls down → 
   184|back neckline pulls up → side varies with arm position
   185|```
   186|
   187|**Pose Descriptions:**
   188|- "V-neck pulled open by fabric weight, chest area revealed by gravity"
   189|- "Round neckline shifted forward by posture, collarbone visible"
   190|- "Neckline stretching as body leans forward, gap increasing"
   191|- "Back neckline lifted by posture, skin exposed at upper back"
   192|
   193|**Avoid:** "low-cut top" (use physics: "neckline stretched by leaning forward")
   194|
   195|---
   196|
   197|### 9. GARMENT SEPARATION FROM BODY
   198|
   199|**Physics Logic:**
   200|```
   201|Arm raises → body moves → fabric stays or follows slowly → 
   202|gap created between fabric and skin → air visible in gap → 
   203|light enters space → shadow on far side of gap
   204|```
   205|
   206|**Pose Descriptions:**
   207|- "Shirt lifting away from torso, air gap visible, light entering space"
   208|- "Arm raised creating space between dress and body, gap shadow visible"
   209|- "Body turned, fabric not yet followed, gap between hip and skirt"
   210|- "Movement creating separation, fabric catching up, light in gap"
   211|
   212|---
   213|
   214|### 10. LAYER INTERACTION
   215|
   216|**Physics Logic:**
   217|```
   218|Two layers → upper layer rests on lower → weight creates compression →
   219|lower layer shows through upper's openings → different movement speeds → 
   220|upper shifts more with motion, lower follows body
   221|```
   222|
   223|**Pose Descriptions:**
   224|- "Cardigan over camisole, weight of knit compressing silk beneath"
   225|- "Blazer over dress, fabric bunching where arm contacts body"
   226|- "Sheer overshirt over solid tank, visible layers with shadow between"
   227|- "Two fabrics at different tensions, upper looser, lower clinging"
   228|
   229|---
   230|
   231|## GARMENT PHYSICS INTEGRATION RULES
   232|
   233|### Rule 1: Explain the WHY
   234|
   235|```
   236|BAD: "Open cardigan, visible shirt"
   237|GOOD: "Cardigan hanging open from own weight, inner shirt visible through gap"
   238|```
   239|
   240|### Rule 2: Use Physics Language
   241|
   242|- Gravity pulls, pools, compresses
   243|- Fabric falls, drapes, clings
   244|- Body creates pressure, contact, gap
   245|- Layers stack, expose, shadow
   246|
   247|### Rule 3: Connect to Pose
   248|
   249|Garment behavior emerges from pose:
   250|- Sitting → skirt displacement
   251|- Reaching → sleeve slippage  
   252|- Turning → fabric separation
   253|- Standing → pooling at hem
   254|
   255|### Rule 4: Include Weight
   256|
   257|Clothing has weight. Heavier fabrics behave differently than light fabrics:
   258|- Heavy knit → less movement, more drape
   259|- Light chiffon → more movement, more cling
   260|- Elastic → compression, contouring
   261|
   262|### Rule 5: Avoid Fetish Framing
   263|
   264|**This is adult fashion realism, not fetish content.**
   265|
   266|```
   267|BAD: "clinging wet fabric emphasizing curves"
   268|GOOD: "wet fabric heavier, clinging to body contour from rain"
   269|
   270|BAD: "sheer fabric showing body"
   271|GOOD: "thin fabric following body curve, skin tone visible through fabric"
   272|```
   273|
   274|---
   275|
   276|## COMPOUND GARMENT PHYSICS EXAMPLES
   277|
   278|### Post-Rain Beach Scene
   279|```
   280|FABRIC: Shirt wet from rain → heavier than normal → gravity pulls more → 
   281|fabric clings tighter to torso → darkens with water absorption → 
   282|sheer areas become more transparent → movement restricted
   283|→ VISUAL: "wet shirt clinging from rain, fabric heavier, clinging to body, darker, more revealing"
   284|```
   285|
   286|### Hotel Morning Layering
   287|```
   288|FABRIC: Post-shower robe + thin camisole underneath → 
   289|robe open at front → camisole visible → robe draping off shoulders → 
   290|camisole thin and clinging → robe heavy and falling
   291|→ VISUAL: "hotel robe open, heavy fabric draping off shoulder, thin camisole visible beneath"
   292|```
   293|
   294|### Late Night Fabric Relaxation
   295|```
   296|FABRIC: She's been wearing dress all day → fabric fatigued → 
   297|less snapback → more draping → wrinkles accumulated → 
   298|body indentations visible in fabric
   299|→ VISUAL: "dress showing wear, fabric less structured, wrinkled from hours of wear"
   300|```
   301|
   302|---
   303|
   304|## FABRIC WEIGHT VOCABULARY
   305|
   306|| Weight | Behavior | Visual |
   307||--------|----------|--------|
   308|| Very light | Floats, billows, moves with air | Chiffon, organza |
   309|| Light | Soft drape, minimal body contact | Silk, thin cotton |
   310|| Medium | Follows body, some movement | Cotton, linen, jersey |
   311|| Heavy | Drapes heavily, pulls open, pools | Wool, velvet, denim |
   312|| Stretch | Contours tightly, elastic compression | Spandex, lycra, swimsuit |
   313|
   314|---
   315|
   316|## ANTI-AI COMPOUND
   317|
   318|```
   319|GARMENT-01 (Physics vocabulary) + FAB-01 (Weather causation)
   320|→ Rain makes fabric wet + heavy + clinging
   321|
   322|GARMENT-02 (Layer interaction) + COL-02 (Fuji Pro 400H)
   323|→ Layered fabric with dreamy rendering
   324|
   325|GARMENT-03 (Gap creation) + MEM-02 (Motion contamination)
   326|→ Body moving, fabric lagging, gap visible
   327|
   328|GARMENT-04 (Fabric fatigue) + EXIST-01 (Photo existence)
   329|→ Worn fabric proves the existence reason (long day, long event)
   330|```
   331|
   332|---
   333|
   334|## QUICK REFERENCE CARD
   335|
   336|**When generating garments:** Ask — "Why does this fabric look this way?"
   337|
   338|**Physics vocabulary to use:**
   339|- Pulls, hangs, drapes, pools, clings
   340|- Compresses, stretches, gaps, shadows
   341|- Heavy, light, tired, settled
   342|- Follows, lags, lifts, separates
   343|
   344|**Connect to:**
   345|- Body pose (sitting = displacement)
   346|- Gravity (standing = pooling)
   347|- Weather (rain = wet + heavy)
   348|- Time (hours = fatigue)
   349|
   350|---
   351|
   352|*End of GARMENT_PHYSICS_LIBRARY.md*
   353|

## V17 FILM STOCK LIBRARY
### Source: modules/V17/FILM_STOCK_LIBRARY.md
================================================================================

     1|# FILM STOCK LIBRARY
     2|### V17 — Fujifilm, Gravure, and Japanese Photobook Rendering
     3|### Status: ACTIVE — Runtime System
     4|
     5|---
     6|
     7|## PHILOSOPHY
     8|
     9|**Core Problem:** AI-generated images look like AI renders — too clean, too saturated, wrong color science. They lack the specific visual language of actual Japanese film photography.
    10|
    11|**The Fix:** Specific film stock vocabulary with actual technical characteristics. Not "film look" but "Fujifilm Pro 400H color science: green push, warm shadow roll, skin with peachy highlight."
    12|
    13|---
    14|
    15|## FUJIFILM PRO 400H (Discontinued 2012)
    16|
    17|### The Signature Japanese Look
    18|
    19|**Color Science:**
    20|```
    21|HIGHLIGHTS: Slightly warm with yellow push
    22|SKIN: Peach-cream undertone, never orange
    23|SHADOWS: Cool magenta shift, never blue
    24|GREEN: Slightly desaturated, olive undertone
    25|WHITE: Cream, not pure
    26|```
    27|
    28|**Technical Characteristics:**
    29|```
    30|GRAIN: Very fine, tight, barely visible at portrait distances
    31|HALATION: Soft, spread into highlights
    32|DYNAMIC RANGE: High, shadows roll off gently
    33|SKIN RENDERING: Signature "glow" — slight light scatter in highlights
    34|CONTRAST: Medium-low, never harsh
    35|```
    36|
    37|**When to Use:**
    38|- Cloudy/overcast light (enhances the peach skin)
    39|- Indoor window light (enhances the glow)
    40|- Skin-forward compositions (maximizes the peach)
    41|- Late Heisei era aesthetic (2000s-2010s)
    42|- Gravure idol aesthetic
    43|
    44|**Prompt Vocabulary:**
    45|```
    46|"Pro 400H color science: peach skin undertone, warm highlight rolloff, 
    47|cool shadow with magenta shift, cream whites, desaturated greens, 
    48|fine grain, soft halo halation, medium-low contrast, skin glow"
    49|```
    50|
    51|---
    52|
    53|## FUJICOLOR C200
    54|
    55|### Casual Japanese Everyday
    56|
    57|**Color Science:**
    58|```
    59|HIGHLIGHTS: Slightly warm, yellow bias
    60|SKIN: Warm peachy, more saturated than Pro 400H
    61|SHADOWS: Slightly green-teal
    62|GREEN: Muted sage, not punchy
    63|OVERALL: Slightly faded, casual snap
    64|```
    65|
    66|**Technical Characteristics:**
    67|```
    68|GRAIN: Fine but visible, adds texture
    69|CONTRAST: Medium, clean
    70|VIVIDNESS: Moderate saturation
    71|FADE: Light natural fade from aging/color degradation
    72|```
    73|
    74|**When to Use:**
    75|- Everyday casual scenes
    76|- Daytime outdoor
    77|- Street photography
    78|- Casual skin tones
    79|- Lower-budget idol photography aesthetic
    80|
    81|**Prompt Vocabulary:**
    82|```
    83|"C200 color: warm peachy skin, slightly faded casual look, 
    84|muted sage green, light grain texture, medium contrast, 
    85|everyday Japanese aesthetic, slight color degradation"
    86|```
    87|
    88|---
    89|
    90|## FUJIFILM SUPERIA PREMIUM 400
    91|
    92|### Late 90s / Early 2000s Japanese
    93|
    94|**Color Science:**
    95|```
    96|HIGHLIGHTS: Warm yellow, slightly blown
    97|SKIN: Warm tan, healthy glow
    98|SHADOWS: Neutral to slight cyan
    99|GREEN: Punchy grass green (Superia strength)
   100|OVERALL: Bright, cheerful, consumer-friendly
   101|```
   102|
   103|**Technical Characteristics:**
   104|```
   105|GRAIN: Medium fine
   106|CONTRAST: Medium-high, punchy
   107|VIVIDNESS: High saturation for consumer film
   108|EDGE: Slightly sharpening
   109|```
   110|
   111|**When to Use:**
   112|- 90s/2000s nostalgic scenes
   113|- Beach/pool scenes (high green)
   114|- Sunny outdoor days
   115|- Cheerful warm mood
   116|- Y2K aesthetic
   117|
   118|**Prompt Vocabulary:**
   119|```
   120|"Superia Premium: warm tan skin, punchy grass green, 
   121|bright cheerful palette, medium grain, medium-high contrast, 
   122|90s-2000s Japanese aesthetic, slightly yellow highlights"
   123|```
   124|
   125|---
   126|
   127|## KODAK GOLD 200
   128|
   129|### Warm Nostalgic Golden Hour
   130|
   131|**Color Science:**
   132|```
   133|HIGHLIGHTS: Golden warm, amber push
   134|SKIN: Warm honey, golden undertone
   135|SHADOWS: Warm brown, no cool
   136|GREEN: Yellow-green, muted
   137|OVERALL: Rich warm saturation, nostalgic
   138|```
   139|
   140|**Technical Characteristics:**
   141|```
   142|GRAIN: Medium, visible texture
   143|CONTRAST: Medium-high, rich
   144|VIVIDNESS: High warmth
   145|HALATION: Orange halos in highlights
   146|FADE: Tends toward warmer fade over time
   147|```
   148|
   149|**When to Use:**
   150|- Late afternoon golden hour
   151|- Warm skin tones
   152|- Nostalgic moments
   153|- Indoor tungsten mixed
   154|- Beach sunset scenes
   155|
   156|**Prompt Vocabulary:**
   157|```
   158|"Gold 200: golden amber warmth, honey skin undertone, 
   159|warm brown shadows, yellow-green muted greens, 
   160|medium grain, high warmth, nostalgic rich saturation, 
   161|orange halation in highlights"
   162|```
   163|
   164|---
   165|
   166|## KODAK PORTRA 400
   167|
   168|### Professional Skin Tone Master
   169|
   170|**Color Science:**
   171|```
   172|HIGHLIGHTS: Neutral to slight warm
   173|SKIN: Perfect natural, slight pink undertone
   174|SHADOWS: Neutral with slight cyan
   175|GREEN: Neutral olive
   176|OVERALL: Clean, professional, versatile
   177|```
   178|
   179|**Technical Characteristics:**
   180|```
   181|GRAIN: Very fine, creamy texture
   182|CONTRAST: Low-medium,宽容度高
   183|DYNAMIC RANGE: Wide, shadow/highlight retention
   184|SKIN: The gold standard for skin
   185|```
   186|
   187|**When to Use:**
   188|- Professional portrait situations
   189|- Natural skin accuracy needed
   190|- Any lighting condition
   191|- Modern casual aesthetic
   192|- When Pro 400H is too dreamy
   193|
   194|**Prompt Vocabulary:**
   195|```
   196|"Portra 400: natural skin with pink undertone, neutral highlights, 
   197|cyan shadow tint, wide dynamic range, very fine grain, 
   198|low-medium contrast, professional clean aesthetic"
   199|```
   200|
   201|---
   202|
   203|## JAPANESE GRAVURE PHOTOBOOK RENDERING
   204|
   205|### Late Heisei (1990s-2019) Visual Language
   206|
   207|**Core Characteristics:**
   208|```
   209|SKIN: Soft focus on skin, slight blur, creamy
   210|EYES: Clear focus, emphasized lashes
   211|HAIR: Slightly darker than reality, soft
   212|LIGHT: Soft diffused window light dominant
   213|COMPOSITION: Centered, face-forward, intimate
   214|OVERALL: Dreamy, soft, romantic, not clinical
   215|```
   216|
   217|**Technical Notes:**
   218|```
   219|LENS: 85mm-135mm portrait primes
   220|APERTURE: Wide (f/1.4-f/2.8) for shallow DOF
   221|FOCUS: Eyes always sharp, skin soft
   222|BAYER: Slight color fringing in corners
   223|POST: Softness, skin smoothing, warm tint
   224|```
   225|
   226|**Specific Look Elements:**
   227|- **Skin:** Porcelain quality, slightly airbrushed, never harsh
   228|- **Eyes:** Clear iris detail, emphasized, slightly brightened
   229|- **Lips:** Slightly pinker than natural, soft highlight
   230|- **Cheeks:** Gentle rosy blush from light, not makeup
   231|- **Nose:** Soft, shadow never harsh
   232|- **Background:** Strong bokeh or pure white/cream
   233|
   234|**When to Use:**
   235|- Gravure aesthetic
   236|- Idol photography style
   237|- Romantic intimate moments
   238|- Beauty-forward compositions
   239|- Hotel/indoor intimate scenes
   240|
   241|**Prompt Vocabulary:**
   242|```
   243|"Gravure photobook: soft focus skin, creamy porcelain quality, 
   244|sharp clear eyes with emphasized lashes, soft diffused window light, 
   245|centered face-forward composition, dreamy romantic tone, 
   246|slight warm tint, gentle bokeh background, beauty-forward"
   247|```
   248|
   249|---
   250|
   251|## LATE HEISEI PHOTobook COLOR SCIENCE
   252|
   253|### 2000s-2019 Japanese Color Trends
   254|
   255|**Phase 1: Mid-2000s (2000-2007)**
   256|```
   257|TENDENCY: Warm, golden, saturated
   258|SKIN: Golden tan, healthy glow
   259|PALETTE: Warm browns, golden yellows
   260|REFERENCE: Similar to Gold 200 aesthetic
   261|```
   262|
   263|**Phase 2: Late 2000s (2008-2012)**
   264|```
   265|TENDENCY: Neutral-cool, professional
   266|SKIN: Natural, slight pink (Portra influence)
   267|PALETTE: Balanced, sophisticated
   268|REFERENCE: More Portra 400 characteristics
   269|```
   270|
   271|**Phase 3: Early 2010s (2013-2019)**
   272|```
   273|TENDENCY: Soft, pastel, dreamy
   274|SKIN: Pale, cool undertone, Pro 400H influence
   275|PALETTE: Lavender, soft pink, muted blue
   276|REFERENCE: Pro 400H peak era
   277|```
   278|
   279|**When to Reference:**
   280|- Historical accuracy for era
   281|- Specific Heisei moment
   282|- Japanese visual culture research
   283|- Authentic period reconstruction
   284|
   285|---
   286|
   287|## SPECIFIC TECHNICAL TERMS
   288|
   289|### Grain Patterns
   290|
   291|| Film | Grain Character | Texture |
   292||------|-----------------|---------|
   293|| Pro 400H | Very fine, tight | Creamy |
   294|| C200 | Fine, visible | Organic |
   295|| Gold 200 | Medium, visible | Warm |
   296|| Portra 400 | Very fine, smooth | Clean |
   297|
   298|**Prompt for grain:**
   299|```
   300|"[FILM] grain: [fine/medium/visible], [tight/organic/warm] texture, 
   301|[creamy/organic/clean] feel"
   302|```
   303|
   304|### Halation
   305|
   306|**What it is:** Light blooming around bright areas (sun, highlights)
   307|
   308|| Film | Halation Character |
   309||------|-------------------|
   310|| Pro 400H | Soft, warm orange, gentle spread |
   311|| Gold 200 | Orange-amber, medium spread |
   312|| CineStill 800T | Orange glow (removable remjet) |
   313|
   314|**Prompt for halation:**
   315|```
   316|"Soft halation around bright areas, warm orange spread, 
   317|gentle glow into shadow areas"
   318|```
   319|
   320|### Highlight Roll-off
   321|
   322|**What it is:** How highlights transition to blown areas
   323|
   324|| Film | Roll-off Character |
   325||------|-------------------|
   326|| Pro 400H | Gentle, creamy, never harsh |
   327|| Portra 400 | Smooth, wide latitude |
   328|| Gold 200 | Warm, slightly punchy |
   329|| C200 | Moderate, consumer-friendly |
   330|
   331|### Shadow Behavior
   332|
   333|| Film | Shadow Character |
   334||------|-----------------|
   335|| Pro 400H | Cool magenta, soft |
   336|| Portra 400 | Neutral-cyan, clean |
   337|| Gold 200 | Warm brown, rich |
   338|| C200 | Slight green-teal |
   339|
   340|---
   341|
   342|## FILM STOCK INTEGRATION RULES
   343|
   344|### Rule 1: Match Film to Lighting Condition
   345|
   346|```
   347|OVERCAST: Pro 400H (enhances peach skin)
   348|GOLDEN HOUR: Gold 200 (maximizes warmth)
   349|INDOOR WINDOW: Pro 400H (window light ideal)
   350|TUNGSTEN NIGHT: CineStill 800T (orange/blue war)
   351|CLOUDY DAY: C200 (casual everyday)
   352|```
   353|
   354|### Rule 2: Include Technical Specifics
   355|
   356|```
   357|BAD: "Film look"
   358|GOOD: "Pro 400H: peach skin undertone, cool magenta shadows, 
   359|       fine tight grain, soft halation, medium-low contrast"
   360|```
   361|
   362|### Rule 3: Match Film to Era/Mood
   363|
   364|```
   365|90s NOSTALGIA: Superia Premium
   366|2000s CASUAL: C200
   367|2000s DREAMY: Pro 400H
   368|MODERN: Portra 400
   369|GRAVURE: Pro 400H + soft focus
   370|```
   371|
   372|### Rule 4: Combine with Spatial + Existence
   373|
   374|```
   375|FILM: Pro 400H + EXISTENCE: hotel mirror check + SPATIAL: foreground perfume bottle
   376|→ Gravure photobook aesthetic + believable photo reason + spatial depth
   377|```
   378|
   379|### Rule 5: Anti-AI Specific Corrections
   380|
   381|**Pro 400H anti-AI markers:**
   382|- Cool shadow magenta (stops blue-correction tendency)
   383|- Peach skin (stops orange-correction tendency)
   384|- Soft halation (stops clean highlight tendency)
   385|- Fine grain (stops perfect-smooth tendency)
   386|
   387|**C200 anti-AI markers:**
   388|- Slight color fade (stops over-saturated tendency)
   389|- Muted green (stops punchy-green tendency)
   390|- Casual tone (stops professional-perfect tendency)
   391|
   392|---
   393|
   394|## FILM STOCK QUICK REFERENCE
   395|
   396|| Scene | Film Stock | Key Markers |
   397||-------|-----------|-------------|
   398|| Cloudy outdoor | Pro 400H | Peach skin, magenta shadow, soft |
   399|| Golden hour | Gold 200 | Amber warmth, honey skin, orange halo |
   400|| Indoor window | Pro 400H | Glow, peach, soft |
   401|| Night street | CineStill 800T | Tungsten orange, blue shadow war |
   402|| Casual everyday | C200 | Warm peachy, faded, muted green |
   403|| Professional | Portra 400 | Natural pink skin, cyan shadow, clean |
   404|| Gravure | Pro 400H + soft | Porcelain skin, sharp eyes, dreamy |
   405|| 90s nostalgia | Superia | Punchy green, tan skin, bright |
   406|| Late Heisei | Pro 400H | Pastel, dreamy, lavender tint |
   407|
   408|---
   409|
   410|## ANTI-AI COMPOUND
   411|
   412|```
   413|FILM-01 (Specific film stock) + SPATIAL-01 (Three-zone depth)
   414|→ Film rendering with spatial depth
   415|
   416|FILM-02 (Pro 400H) + GARMENT-01 (Physics vocabulary)
   417|→ Dreamy film + realistic fabric behavior
   418|
   419|FILM-03 (Film + era) + EXIST-01 (Photo existence)
   420|→ Era-appropriate film for believable photo reason
   421|
   422|FILM-04 (Gravure) + EYE-01 (Eye flow)
   423|→ Beauty-forward composition with visual path
   424|```
   425|
   426|---
   427|
   428|*End of FILM_STOCK_LIBRARY.md*
